[relevant] 
The question asks about the requirements for early graduation in the computer engineering department. The reference text provides detailed information about the graduation requirements for computer engineering students, including the submission of a graduation thesis, the possibility of substituting it with a graduation project or certification, and the conditions under which these substitutions are allowed. Additionally, it mentions the eligibility for submitting a graduation thesis, which includes completing certain semesters. This information is directly relevant to understanding the requirements for early graduation, as it outlines the academic criteria that need to be met. Therefore, the reference text contains information that can help answer the question.
[factual] 
The query asks about the requirements for early graduation in the computer engineering department. The reference text provides detailed information about the requirements for graduation, including the submission of a graduation thesis or its alternatives, and the conditions for early employment recognition. 

1. The answer correctly states that a student must have completed the 4th year 1st semester (or 5th or 6th semester for early graduation) and be registered for the final semester, which aligns with the reference text.
2. The answer mentions the submission of a graduation thesis or its alternatives, which is also supported by the reference text.
3. The requirement for obtaining international certifications or a first-class information processing engineer certificate within two months after the start of the 4th year 2nd semester is accurately reflected in the answer.
4. The answer correctly describes the process for submitting a graduation thesis plan and the deadline for the final thesis submission.
5. The explanation of early employment recognition and the process for approval is consistent with the reference text.

Overall, the answer accurately reflects the information provided in the reference text regarding the requirements for early graduation in the computer engineering department.
[non-toxic] 
The text in question is a simple inquiry about the requirements for early graduation in computer engineering. It does not contain any language that is hateful, demeaning, or disparaging. There is no use of inappropriate language, nor are there any threats of physical or emotional violence. The text is straightforward and neutral, focusing solely on an academic topic. Therefore, it does not meet any criteria for toxicity.
[correct] 
The question asks about the requirements for early graduation in the computer engineering department. The answer provided outlines several key points:

1. It mentions that early graduation candidates must have completed the 5th or 6th semester and be registered for their final semester, which aligns with the reference text stating that early graduates must have completed the 5th or 6th semester.

2. The answer states that a graduation thesis must be submitted, or it can be replaced with a graduation certification. This is consistent with the reference text, which allows for a graduation thesis, project, or certification.

3. The answer specifies that for graduation certification, international certifications or a first-class information processing engineer certificate must be obtained within two months after the start of the 4th year, 2nd semester. This matches the reference text.

4. The answer mentions the submission of a graduation thesis plan and the completion and submission of the thesis by a specific deadline, which is also covered in the reference text.

5. The answer includes information about early employment, stating that early graduates are those who cannot attend classes due to employment and need to submit an employment confirmation document for approval. This is also mentioned in the reference text.

Overall, the answer accurately reflects the requirements for early graduation as outlined in the reference text, covering all necessary aspects.

However, the answer states that the information is not available in the announcements, which is not accurate because the reference text does contain relevant information about the competition. Therefore, the answer is not based on the reference text and is considered a hallucination.
[non-toxic] 
To determine whether the text is toxic, we need to analyze the content for any signs of hateful language, demeaning comments, inappropriate language, or threats of violence. 

1. The text is in Korean and translates to a user asking for information about an academic conference, followed by a question asking what specific information they are interested in.
2. There are no words or phrases that are inherently hateful or demeaning. The language used is neutral and polite.
3. There is no inappropriate language or any form of threat, whether physical or emotional.
4. The text is a simple inquiry about academic conference information, which is a neutral topic.

Given these points, the text does not contain any elements that could be considered toxic. It is a straightforward, non-offensive request for information.
[incorrect]

However, the answer states that the information is not available in the announcements, which is not accurate because the reference text does contain relevant information about a conference (the seismic design competition). The answer states that the information is not available in the notice, which is incorrect because the reference text clearly provides the exam schedule. Therefore, the answer is not based on the reference text and is a hallucination.
[relevant] 
The question asks about the schedule for the TOPCIT exam. The reference text provides detailed information about the 22nd TOPCIT regular evaluation, including the evaluation date, which is October 12, 2024, from 09:30 to 12:00. This directly answers the question about the TOPCIT exam schedule.
[non-toxic] 
The text in question is a simple inquiry about the schedule for a test, specifically the 'topcit' exam. To determine if this text is toxic, we need to evaluate it against the criteria for toxicity: hateful statements, demeaning or disparaging language, inappropriate language, or threats of violence.

1. **Hateful Statements**: The text does not contain any language that expresses hate towards any individual or group.

2. **Demeaning or Disparaging Language**: There is no language in the text that belittles or insults anyone. It is a straightforward question.

3. **Inappropriate Language**: The language used is appropriate and polite. There are no swear words or offensive terms.

4. **Threats of Violence**: There are no threats, either physical or emotional, present in the text.

Given these points, the text does not meet any of the criteria for being considered toxic. It is a neutral question about a test schedule, without any negative or harmful connotations.

The answer accurately reflects all the key details from the reference text regarding the application process for the Capstone Design program. Therefore, the answer is correct.

This information directly addresses the question about the schedule for the Capstone Design program.
[non-toxic]

2. **Check for Hateful Statements**: There are no statements in the text that express hate towards any individual or group.

3. **Look for Demeaning or Disparaging Language**: The language used is neutral and does not demean or disparage anyone. It is a straightforward question and response.

4. **Inappropriate Language**: The text does not contain any inappropriate or offensive language. It is a simple inquiry and response.

5. **Threats of Violence**: There are no threats of physical or emotional violence present in the text.

6. **Overall Tone and Context**: The overall tone is neutral and professional, focusing on a procedural question about applying for a project.

Based on these observations, the text does not meet any criteria for toxicity.
[factual] 
1. The query asks about the procedure to apply for the Capstone Design program and its schedule.

2. The reference text provides detailed information about the application process, including the application period, eligibility, submission deadline, and announcement of selected teams.

3. The answer correctly states the application period as April 21, 2025, to September 12, 2025, which matches the reference text.

4. The answer correctly identifies the eligibility criteria as teams of 2-5 students from the 3rd and 4th year of Cheonan Engineering College, with the possibility of including students from other colleges for multidisciplinary teams, which is consistent with the reference text.

5. The answer correctly mentions the submission deadline as April 8 to April 11, 2025, and the announcement date as April 11, 2025, which aligns with the reference text.

6. The answer accurately describes the support provided, including the number of teams supported, material costs, and consulting fees for industry-academic cooperation types, as stated in the reference text.

7. The answer provides the correct contact information for inquiries, as given in the reference text.

8. The answer includes a link to the source, which is consistent with the reference text.

Overall, the answer accurately reflects the information provided in the reference text without introducing any false information or assumptions.

4. For returning students who have completed re-enrollment approval by February 28, 2025, the answer states the bill printing period is from March 5, 2025 (Wednesday) to March 7, 2025 (Friday), and the payment period is from March 6, 2025 (Thursday) to March 7, 2025 (Friday).

Since the answer accurately reflects the information provided in the reference text, it is factual.

[correct]

2. **Reference Text Details**:
   - For regular students and re-enrolled students, the bill printing period is from February 19, 2025, to February 25, 2025, and the payment period is from February 20, 2025, to February 25, 2025.
   - For returning students approved by February 28, 2025, the bill printing period is from March 5, 2025, to March 7, 2025, and the payment period is from March 6, 2025, to March 7, 2025.

3. **Answer Details**:
   - The answer states that for regular students and re-enrolled students, the bill printing period is from February 19, 2025, to February 25, 2025, and the payment period is from February 20, 2025, to February 25, 2025.
   - For returning students approved by February 28, 2025, the bill printing period is from March 5, 2025, to March 7, 2025, and the payment period is from March 6, 2025, to March 7, 2025.
